60 §1402. Legislative intent; declaration of purpose and policy
61 It is the intent of the legislature to protect the health, safety, and well-being
62 of the children and youth of the state who are in out-of-home care on a regular or
Page 61 of 111

SCASB462 3005 1692
1 consistent basis. Toward that end, it is the purpose of this Chapter to establish
2 statewide minimum standards for the safety and well-being of children and youth,
3 to ensure maintenance of these standards, and to regulate conditions in these
4 facilities through a program of licensing. It shall be the policy of the state to ensure
5 protection of all individuals under care by specialized providers and to encourage
6 and assist in the improvement of programs. It is the further intent of the legislature
7 that the freedom of religion of all citizens shall be inviolate. This Chapter shall not
8 give the Louisiana Department of Health and Human Services or the Department
9 of Children and Family Services jurisdiction or authority to regulate, control,
10 supervise, or in any way be involved in the form, manner, or content of any
11 curriculum or instruction of a school or specialized provider sponsored by a church
12 or religious organization so long as the civil and human rights of the clients and
13 residents are not violated.

13 §1430. Operating in violation of regulations; penalties and fines

16 to report critical incidents, the Louisiana Department of Children and Family
17 Services Health and Human Services may issue a written warning that includes a
18 corrective action plan, in lieu of revocation, upon any person or specialized provider
19 violating these requirements if such condition or occurrence does not pose an
20 imminent threat to the health, safety, rights, or welfare of a child. Failure to
21 implement a corrective action plan issued pursuant to this Section may result in
22 either the assessment of a civil fine or license revocation or may result in both
23 actions being taken by the department. Such civil fine shall not exceed two hundred
24 fifty dollars per day for each assessment; however, the aggregate fines assessed for
25 violations determined in any consecutive twelve-month period shall not exceed two
26 thousand dollars.

43 §1844. Basic rights for victim and witness
44 * * *
45 W. Confidentiality of crime victims who are minors, victims of sex offenses,
46 and victims of human trafficking-related offenses.
47 (1)(a) In order to protect the identity and provide for the safety and welfare
48 of crime victims who are minors under the age of eighteen years and of victims of
49 sex offenses or human trafficking-related offenses, notwithstanding any provision
50 of law to the contrary, all public officials and officers and public agencies, including
51 but not limited to all law enforcement agencies, sheriffs, district attorneys, judicial
52 officers, clerks of court, the Crime Victims Reparations Board, and the Louisiana
53 Department of Children and Family Services Health and Human Services or any
54 division thereof, shall not publicly disclose the name, address, contact information,
55 or identity of crime victims who at the time of the commission of the offense are
56 minors under eighteen years of age or of victims of sex offenses or human
57 trafficking-related offenses, regardless of the date of commission of the offense. The
58 confidentiality of the identity of the victim who at the time of the commission of the
59 offense is a minor under eighteen years of age or the victim of a sex offense or
60 human trafficking-related offense may be waived by the victim. The public
61 disclosure of the name of the juvenile crime victim by any public official or officer
62 or public agency is not prohibited by this Subsection when the crime resulted in the
Page 64 of 111

SCASB462 3005 1692
1 death of the victim. Nothing in this Subsection shall be construed to require the
2 redaction of a victim's name when the named victim is the one requesting such
3 documents, reports, or any other records.
4 * * *
5 (3) Notwithstanding any other provision of law to the contrary, all public
6 officials, officers, and public agencies, including but not limited to all law
7 enforcement agencies, sheriffs, district attorneys, judicial officers, clerks of court,
8 the Crime Victims Reparations Board, and the Louisiana Department of Children
9 and Family Services Health and Human Services or any division thereof, charged
10 with the responsibility of knowing the name, address, contact information, and
11 identity of crime victims who are minors or of crime victims of a sex offense or a
12 human trafficking-related offense as a necessary part of their duties shall have full
13 and complete access to this information regarding a crime victim who is a minor or
14 a victim of a sex offense or a human trafficking-related offense. Either prior to or at
15 the time of a request for information, the public official or officer or public agency
16 shall take measures to prevent the public disclosure of the name, address, contact
17 information, or identity of such a crime victim who is a minor or a victim of a sex
18 offense or human trafficking-related offense, which may include the use of initials,
19 abbreviations, or any other form of concealing the identity of the victim on all public
20 documents.
21 * * *
22 (5)(a) In order to provide for the safety and welfare of victims of crimes
23 against family members, household members, or dating partners, notwithstanding
24 any provision of law to the contrary, all public officials and officers and public
25 agencies, including but not limited to all law enforcement agencies, sheriffs, district
26 attorneys, judicial officers, clerks of court, the Crime Victims Reparations Board,
27 and the Louisiana Department of Children and Family Services Health and Human
28 Services or any division thereof, shall not publicly disclose the address or contact
29 information of victims of crimes against family members, household members, or
30 dating partners. The confidentiality of the address and contact information of the
31 victim of a crime against a family member, household member, or dating partner
32 may be waived by the victim.
33 * * *
34 (c) Notwithstanding any other provision of law to the contrary, all public
35 officials, officers, and public agencies, including but not limited to all law
36 enforcement agencies, sheriffs, district attorneys, judicial officers, clerks of court,
37 the Crime Victims Reparations Board, and the Louisiana Department of Children
38 and Family Services Health and Human Services or any division thereof, charged
39 with the responsibility of knowing the address and contact information of victims of
40 crimes against family members, household members, or dating partners as a
41 necessary part of their duties shall have full and complete access to this information
42 regarding a victim of a crime against a family member, household member, or dating
43 partner. Either prior to or at the time of a request for information, the public official
44 or officer or public agency shall take measures to prevent the public disclosure of the
45 address and contact information of a victim of a crime against a family member,
46 household member, or dating partner.
47 * * *
48 §1906.2. Interdepartmental cooperation
49 The Department of Public Safety and Corrections, Department of Children
50 and Family Services, Louisiana Department of Health and Human Services,
51 Department of Education, and the Juvenile and Family Court Judges Association
52 shall consult and cooperate to develop a plan for treatment and a continuum of care
53 for children alleged to be or adjudicated delinquent or in need of care or supervision.
54 The purposes of such consultation shall include the goal of early intervention by the
55 components of the juvenile justice system to assist children in receiving proper
56 treatment so that they will be less likely to re-enter the system.

38 this information to the legislature on or before the first day of February each year.

38 §2552. Prevention of teen pregnancy and sexually transmitted diseases; agency
39 cooperation
40 A. The state superintendent of education, the secretary of the Department of
41 Children and Family Services, and the secretary of the Louisiana Department of
42 Health and Human Services shall meet together not less than twice annually to
43 review and evaluate the effectiveness of current state programs, including but not
44 limited to sex education provided by public schools, aimed at reducing the rate of
45 teen pregnancy and preventing the spread of HIV and other sexually transmitted
46 diseases among the youth of Louisiana.
47 B. The state superintendent of education, the secretary of the Department of
48 Children and Family Services, and the secretary of the Louisiana Department of
49 Health and Human Services shall review and evaluate any programs that are
50 available for implementation in Louisiana to educate the youth of Louisiana about
51 the importance of preventing teen pregnancy and the spread of HIV and other
52 sexually transmitted diseases by providing culturally competent education and
53 outreach.
54 §2553. Report
55 The state superintendent of education, the secretary of the Department of
56 Children and Family Services, and the secretary of the Louisiana Department of
57 Health and Human Services, jointly, shall submit a written report of their findings
58 and recommendations, including proposed legislation if necessary, for a
59 comprehensive strategy to reduce the rate of teen pregnancy and prevent the spread
60 of HIV and other sexually transmitted diseases among the youth of Louisiana on an
61 annual basis to the legislature not later than sixty days prior to the commencement
62 of the regular legislative session. Any recommendations made by the state

15 §6105. Child care provider tax credit
16 A. There shall be a credit against any Louisiana income tax for a child care
17 provider. The tax credit shall be refundable as provided for in R.S. 47:6108. The tax
18 credit shall be an amount based upon the average monthly number of children who
19 either participate in the Child Care Assistance Program administered by the state
20 Department of Education or who are foster children in the custody of the Louisiana
21 Department of Children and Family Services Health and Human Services, and who
22 are attending a child care facility or facilities operated by the child care provider,
23 multiplied by an amount which shall be based upon the quality rating of each child
24 care facility operated by the child care provider as follows:
25 Quality Rating of Child Care FacilityTax Credit Per Eligible Child Attending
26 Five star $1,500
27 Four star $1,250
28 Three star $1,000
29 Two star $750
30 One star or nonparticipating facility 0

12 Art. 683. Unemancipated minor
13 * * *
14 D. Notwithstanding the provisions of Paragraph A, B, or C of this Article, an
15 attorney appointed by the court having jurisdiction over an unemancipated minor
16 who is in the legal custody of the Louisiana Department of Children and Family
17 Services Health and Human Services is the proper plaintiff to sue to enforce a right

22 attorney.

30 enforce an obligation against an unemancipated minor. Upon application of the tutor
31 or person having parental authority who would otherwise be the proper defendant to
32 be sued pursuant to Paragraph B or C of this Article, the court shall appoint or
33 substitute as the proper defendant the best qualified among the tutor, a person having
34 parental authority, or the appointed attorney.

6 trust qualified under 42 U.S.C. 1396p(d)(4)(C) in accordance with the law of any
7 state. The trust instrument shall name the minor as sole beneficiary of the trust, shall
8 name a trustee, shall impose maximum spendthrift restraints, and may allow the trust
9 to last for the lifetime of the beneficiary. Except for trusts qualified under 42 U.S.C.
10 1396p(d)(4)(A) or 1396p(d)(4)(C), the trust shall, however, be subject to termination
11 at the option of the beneficiary upon attaining the age of majority. If the minor fails
12 to attain majority, the trust shall be subject to termination at the option of his heirs
13 or legatees. The court shall not order funds that will be paid to an unemancipated
14 minor who is in the legal custody of the Louisiana Department of Children and
15 Family Services Health and Human Services to be placed in trust if the amount of
16 the judgment or settlement is less than fifty thousand dollars.

4 Art. 603. Definitions
5 As used in this Title:
6 (1) "Abortion" means that the procedure as defined in R.S. 14:87.1.
7 (2) "Abuse" means any one of the following acts that seriously endanger the
8 physical, mental, or emotional health, welfare, and safety of the child:
9 (a) The infliction, attempted infliction, or, as a result of inadequate
10 supervision, the allowance of the infliction or attempted infliction of physical or
11 mental injury upon the child by a parent or any other person.
12 (b) The exploitation or overwork of a child by a parent or any other person,
13 including but not limited to commercial sexual exploitation of the child.
14 (c) The involvement of the child in any sexual act with a parent or any other
15 person, or the aiding or toleration by the parent, caretaker, or any other person of the
16 child's involvement in any of the following:
17 (i) Any sexual act with any other person.
18 (ii) Pornographic displays.
19 (iii) Any sexual activity constituting a crime under the laws of this state.
20 (d) A coerced abortion conducted upon a child.
21 (e) Female genital mutilation as defined by R.S. 14:43.4 of this child or of a
22 sister of the child.
23 (a) Extreme or repeated cruelty to a child.
24 (b) Engaging in conduct creating a realistic and serious threat of death,
25 permanent or temporary disfigurement, or impairment of any bodily organ.
26 (c) Injury to a child's intellectual, emotional, or psychological
27 development as evidenced by observable and substantial impairment of the
28 child's ability to function within the child's normal range of performance and
29 behavior.
30 (d) Any injury that is at variance with the history given.
31 (e) Any nonaccidental physical injury.
32 (f) Any of the following intentional or knowing acts, with physical injury
33 and without justifiable cause:
34 (i)Throwing, kicking, burning, biting, or cutting a child.
35 (ii) Striking a child with a closed fist.
36 (iii) Shaking a child.
37 (iv) Striking a child on the face or head.
38 (g) Any of the following intentional or knowing acts, with or without
39 physical injury:
40 (i) Striking a child six years of age or younger on the face or head.
41 (ii) Shaking a child three years of age or younger.
42 (iii) Interfering with a child's breathing.
43 (iv) Pinching, biting, or striking a child in the genital area.
44 (v) Tying a child to a fixed or heavy object or binding or tying a child's
45 limbs together.
46 (h) Giving a child or permitting a child to consume or inhale a poisonous
47 or noxious substance not prescribed by a physician that has the capacity to
48 interfere with normal physiological functions.
49 (i) Giving a child or permitting a child to consume or inhale a substance
50 not prescribed by a physician that has the capacity to alter the mood of the
51 child, including, but not limited to, the following:
52 (i) Marijuana.
53 (ii) Alcohol, excluding alcohol given to a child during a recognized and
54 established religious ceremony or service.
55 (iii) A narcotic.
56 (iv) An over-the-counter drug if a person purposely administers an
57 overdose to a child or purposely gives an inappropriate over-the-counter drug
58 to a child and the child is detrimentally impacted by the overdose or the
59 over-the-counter drug.
60 (j) Exposing a child to a chemical that has the capacity to interfere with
61 normal physiological functions, including, but not limited to, a chemical used
62 or generated during the manufacture of methamphetamine.
Page 79 of 111

SCASB462 3005 1692
1 (k) Subjecting a child to Munchausen syndrome by proxy or a factitious
2 illness by proxy if the incident is confirmed by medical personnel.
3 (l) Recruiting, harboring, transporting, or obtaining a child for labor or
4 services, through force, fraud, or coercion, for the purpose of subjection to
5 involuntary servitude, peonage, debt bondage, or slavery.
6 (m) Female genital mutilation.
7 (n) The list provided for in this Paragraph shall be considered
8 illustrative of unreasonable action that constitutes abuse and shall not be
9 construed to be exclusive. No unreasonable action shall be construed to permit
10 a finding of abuse without having established the elements of abuse.
11 * * *
12 (11) "Court-appointed or court-approved administrative body" means a body

16 Department of Children and Family Services Health and Human Services or the

19 * * *
20 (13) "Department" means the Louisiana Department of Children and Family
21 Services Health and Human Services.
22 * * *
23 (17) "Mandatory reporter" is any of the following individuals:
24 * * *
25 (o) Any employee of the office of juvenile justice or the Louisiana
26 Department of Children and Family Services Health and Human Services, whose
27 duties include supervisory or disciplinary authority over children.
28 (18) "Neglect" means the refusal or unreasonable failure of a parent or
29 caretaker to supply the child with necessary food, clothing, shelter, care, treatment,
30 or counseling for any injury, illness, or condition of the child, as a result of which the
31 child's physical, mental, or emotional health, welfare, and safety is substantially
32 threatened or impaired. Neglect includes prenatal neglect. Consistent with Article
33 606(B), the inability of a parent or caretaker to provide for a child due to inadequate
34 financial resources shall not, for that reason alone, be considered neglect. Whenever,
35 in lieu of medical care, a child is being provided treatment in accordance with the
36 tenets of a well-recognized religious method of healing that has a reasonable, proven
37 record of success, the child shall not, for that reason alone, be considered to be
38 neglected or maltreated. However, nothing in this Subparagraph shall prohibit the
39 court from ordering medical services for the child when there is substantial risk of
40 harm to the child's health, welfare, or safety. means the act or omission of a parent
41 or caretaker which constitute:
42 (a) Failure or refusal to prevent the abuse of the child when the person
43 knows or has reasonable cause to know the child is or has been abused.
44 (b) Failure or refusal to provide necessary food, clothing, shelter, or
45 medical treatment necessary for the child's well-being, except when the failure
46 or refusal is caused primarily by the financial inability of the person legally
47 responsible and no services for relief have been offered.
48 (c) Failure to take reasonable action to protect the child from
49 abandonment, abuse, sexual abuse, sexual exploitation, or neglect when the
50 existence of the condition was known or should have been known, and, if for
51 abuse or neglect, the failure to take reasonable action to protect the juvenile
52 causes the juvenile serious bodily injury.
53 (d) Failure or irremediable inability to provide for the essential and
54 necessary physical, mental, or emotional needs of the child, including the failure
55 to provide a shelter that does not pose a risk to the health or safety of the child.
56 (e) Failure to provide for the child's care and maintenance, proper or
57 necessary support, or medical, surgical, or other necessary care.
58 (f) Failure, although able, to assume responsibility for the care and
59 custody of the child or to participate in a plan to assume such responsibility.
60 (g) Failure to appropriately supervise the child that results in the child's
61 being left alone:
62 (i) At an inappropriate age creating a dangerous situation.
Page 80 of 111

SCASB462 3005 1692
1 (ii) In inappropriate circumstances creating a dangerous situation.
2 (h) Failure to appropriately supervise the child that results in the child's
3 being placed in inappropriate circumstances creating a dangerous situation.
4 (i) Failure to ensure a child between six years of age and seventeen years
5 of age is enrolled in school or is being legally homeschooled.
6 (j)An act or omission by the parent or caretaker of the child that results
7 in the child's being habitually and without justification absent from school.
8 (k) Causing a child to be born with an illegal substance present in the
9 child's bodily fluids or bodily substances as a result of the pregnant mother's
10 knowingly using an illegal substance before the birth of the child. As used in this
11 Item, "illegal substance" means a drug that is prohibited to be used or
12 possessed without a prescription.
13 (l) At the time of the birth of a child, the presence of an illegal substance
14 in the mother's bodily fluids or bodily substances as a result of the pregnant
15 mother's knowingly using an illegal substance before the birth of the child. A
16 test of the child's bodily fluids or bodily substances may be used as evidence to
17 establish neglect pursuant to this Item. A test of the mother's bodily fluids or
18 bodily substances may be used as evidence to establish neglect pursuant to this
19 Item.
20 (m) Abandonment.
21 * * *
22 (33) "Abandonment" means the failure of a parent to provide reasonable
23 support and to maintain regular contact with a child through statement or
24 contact when the failure is accompanied by an intention on the part of the
25 parent to permit the condition to continue for an indefinite period in the future
26 or the failure of a parent to support or maintain regular contact with a child
27 without just cause, an articulated intent to forego parental responsibility, or
28 refusal to resume parental responsibility and take physical custody of a child
29 after being notified of a medical discharge from a hospital.
30 (34) "Child maltreatment" means abuse, sexual abuse, neglect, sexual
31 exploitation, or abandonment.
32 (35) "Severe maltreatment" means sexual abuse, sexual exploitation, acts
33 or omissions that may or do result in death, abuse involving the use of a deadly
34 weapon, bone fracture, internal injuries, burns, immersions, suffocation,
35 abandonment, medical diagnosis of failure to thrive, or causing a substantial
36 and observable change in the behavior or demeanor of the child.

52 Art. 608. Parents' right to counsel; payment
53 A. The parents of a child who is the subject of a child in need of care
54 proceeding shall be entitled to qualified, independent counsel after the court issues
55 any order in accordance with Article 619(C) or 620 or at the filing of a petition and
56 at all stages of the proceedings thereafter. If the court does not issue an order in
57 accordance with Article 619(C) or 620, the right to counsel shall attach upon the
58 filing of a petition. At all proceedings governed by Chapter 6 of this Title, the
59 parents shall be presumed to be indigent. Thereafter, indigence shall be determined
60 in accordance with Article 320. The right to counsel may be waived by a parent if
61 the court determines that the parent choosing to waive the right to representation has
Page 81 of 111

SCASB462 3005 1692
1 been instructed by the court about the rights and the possible consequences of
2 waiver. Before accepting a waiver of counsel, the court shall ensure each of the
3 following:
4 (1) The parent has been informed by the court that the Louisiana Department
5 of Children and Family Services Health and Human Services cannot provide legal
6 advice to the parent or represent the parent's interest.

8 Art. 609. Mandatory and permitted reporting; training requirements
9 A. With respect to mandatory reporters:
10 * * *
11 (3)(a) To familiarize mandatory reporters, as defined by Children's Code
12 Article 603, with their legal mandate for reporting suspected child abuse and neglect,

20 Art. 610. Reporting procedure; reports to the legislature and the United States
21 Department of Defense Family Advocacy Program
22 A. A reporter shall immediately report suspected child abuse or neglect or
23 that child abuse or neglect was a contributing factor in a child's death in the
24 following ways:
25 (1) To the Department of Children and Family Services if the reporter has
26 reason to believe that the perpetrator is any of the following:
27 (a) A parent or caretaker as defined in Article 603.
28 (b) A person who maintains an interpersonal dating or engagement
29 relationship with the parent or caretaker.
30 (c) A person living in the same residence as the parent or caretaker.
31 (d) A person living in the same residence as the child, or any residence of the
32 child, if the child has more than one residence.
33 (e) An employee or an operator of an early learning center as defined in R.S.
34 17:407.33.
35 (f) An operator or employee of a registered family child day care home.
36 (g) Another child residing in the same residence for cases of suspected sexual
37 abuse.
38 (h) Indeterminable by the mandatory reporter, but the reporter suspects that
39 the abuse occurred at the child's residence.
40 (2) To a local or state law enforcement agency if the reporter has reason to
41 believe that the perpetrator is any of the following:
42 (a) A person other than a person provided for in Subparagraph (1) of this
43 Paragraph.
44 (b) A teacher, instructor, administrator, staff person, school bus driver,
45 teacher aide, paraprofessional, food service worker, or employee of any public or
46 private elementary, secondary, vocational-technical training, special, or
47 postsecondary school, city, parish, or other local public school board, if the abuse or
48 neglect is perpetrated on a student.
49 (c) Another child who does not reside in the same residence for cases of
50 suspected sexual abuse.
51 (3) Dual reporting to both the department and the local or state law
52 enforcement agency is permitted. However, the agency who receives a report
53 pursuant to Subparagraph (1) or (2) of this Paragraph shall be the agency responsible
54 for accepting and acting on the report and shall ensure referral to other agencies as
55 necessary.
56 (4) Reports to the department shall be made as follows:
57 (a) A mandatory reporter shall make a report of suspected abuse or neglect
58 requiring immediate assistance via the designated state child protection reporting
59 hotline telephone number. A report of suspected abuse or neglect which is of a
60 nonemergency nature may be reported via the Louisiana Department of Children and
Page 82 of 111

SCASB462 3005 1692
1 Family Services Mandated Reporter Portal online. Reports may also be made in
2 person at any child welfare office.
3 (b) If a report involves alleged sex trafficking, all mandatory reporters shall
4 report via the hotline telephone number to the department regardless of whether there
5 is alleged parental or caretaker culpability.
6 (c) A permitted reporter shall make a report through the designated state child
7 protection reporting hotline telephone number or in person at any child welfare
8 office.
9 (5) If a school resource officer suspects child abuse or neglect of a student or
10 if a mandatory reporter reports suspected child abuse or neglect to a school resource
11 officer, the school resource officer shall immediately notify the officer's employing
12 law enforcement agency or the Department of Children and Family Services in
13 accordance with the provisions of this Article. The school resource officer's
14 employer shall assign investigation of the matter to the most appropriate law
15 enforcement officer, who may be the school resource officer.
16 (6) If a mandatory reporter is prohibited from immediately making the report
17 required by this Chapter to the department or local or state law enforcement because
18 of an employer's policies or employee manual, the mandatory reporter shall file a
19 complaint with local or state law enforcement. Local or state law enforcement shall
20 investigate the complaint, and an employer violating this Chapter shall be subject to
21 the penalties provided for in R.S. 14:131.1 and 403. An employer shall not
22 discriminate or retaliate against an employee who is a mandatory reporter for
23 complying with this Article. If an employer is found discriminating or retaliating
24 against an employee for complying with this Article, the employer shall be subject
25 to double the fines provided for in R.S. 14:131.1 and 403.
26 (7) In an investigation of a report of abuse or neglect allegedly committed by
27 a parent or caretaker, the department shall determine whether the person is an active
28 duty member of the United States Armed Forces or the spouse of a member on active
29 duty. If the department determines that the person is an active duty member of the
30 United States Armed Forces or the spouse of a member on active duty, the
31 department shall notify the United States Department of Defense Family Advocacy
32 Program at the closest active duty military installation of the investigation.
33 A. There shall be a Child Abuse Hotline established within the office of
34 state police. The Child Abuse Hotline shall be staffed twenty-four hours per day
35 and shall have statewide accessibility through a toll-free telephone number.
36 B. All persons, whether a mandatory reporter or not, may use the Child
37 Abuse Hotline to report child maltreatment or suspected child maltreatment or
38 a secure web based platform.
39 C. A person shall immediately notify the Child Abuse Hotline if he or
40 she:
41 (1) Has reasonable cause to suspect that:
42 (a) Child maltreatment has occurred.
43 (b) A child has died as a result of child maltreatment.
44 (2) Observes a child being subjected to conditions or circumstances that
45 would reasonably result in child maltreatment.
46 B. D. The report shall contain the following information, if known:
47 (1) The name, address, age, sex, and race of the child.
48 (2) The nature, extent, and cause of the child's injuries or endangered
49 condition, including any previous known or suspected abuse to this child or the
50 child's siblings.
51 (3) The name and address of the child's parent(s) or other caretaker.
52 (4) The names and ages of all other members of the child's household.
53 (5) The name and address of the reporter.
54 (6) An account of how this child came to the reporter's attention.
55 (7) Any explanation of the cause of the child's injury or condition offered by
56 the child, the caretaker, or any other person.
57 (8) The number of times the reporter has filed a report on the child or the
58 child's siblings.
59 (9) Any other information which the reporter believes might be important or
60 relevant.
Page 83 of 111

SCASB462 3005 1692
1 C. E.The report shall also name the person or persons who are thought to
2 have caused or contributed to the child's condition, if known, and the report shall
3 contain the name of such person if he is named by the child.
4 F. The Child Abuse Hotline shall accept a report of any allegation of
5 child maltreatment or suspected child maltreatment, that if found to be true,
6 would constitute child maltreatment as defined in this Title.
7 D. If the initial report was in oral form by a mandatory reporter, it shall be
8 followed by a written report made within five days via the online Mandated Reporter
9 Portal of the department or by mail to the centralized intake unit of the department
10 at the address provided on the website of the department; or, if necessary, to the local
11 law enforcement agency. The reporter may use a form for the written report, which
12 shall be developed, approved, and made available by the Department of Children and
13 Family Services. The form is optional and may be available electronically on the
14 department's website.
15 E.(1) All reports made to any local or state law enforcement agency involving
16 abuse or neglect in which an individual provided for in Subparagraph (A)(1) of this
17 Article is believed responsible shall be reported to the department within twenty-four
18 hours in accordance with Paragraph A of this Article.
19 (2) All reports made to the department involving abuse or neglect in which
20 someone other than an individual provided for in Subparagraph (A)(1) of this Article
21 is believed to be responsible shall be reported to the appropriate law enforcement
22 agency within twenty-four hours by telephone. The department also shall report all
23 cases of child death which involve a suspicion of abuse or neglect as a contributing
24 factor in the child's death to the local and state law enforcement agencies, the office
25 of the district attorney, and the coroner.
26 (3) Reports involving a felony-grade crime against a child shall be promptly
27 communicated to the appropriate law enforcement authorities as part of the
28 interagency protocols for multidisciplinary investigations of child abuse and neglect
29 in each judicial district as provided in Articles 509 and 510.
30 (4) The department shall communicate as soon as possible all reports
31 involving alleged child victims of sex trafficking to the Louisiana State Police for
32 referral to the appropriate local law enforcement agency for investigation or other
33 action as appropriate.
34 F. G. Any commercial film or photographic print processor who has
35 knowledge of or observes, within the scope of this professional capacity or
36 employment, any film, photograph, video tape, negative, or slide depicting a child
37 who he knows or should know is under the age of seventeen years, which constitutes
38 child pornography or child sexual abuse materials as defined in Article 603, shall
39 report immediately to the local law enforcement agency having jurisdiction over the
40 case hotline. The reporter shall provide a copy of the film, photograph, videotape,
41 negative, or slide to the law enforcement agency receiving the report.
42 G. H.(1) If a physician has cause to believe that a newborn was exposed in
43 utero to an unlawfully used controlled dangerous substance, as defined by R.S.
44 40:961 et seq., the physician shall order a toxicology test upon the newborn, without
45 the consent of the newborn's parents or guardian, to determine whether there is
46 evidence of prenatal neglect. If the test results are positive, the physician shall issue
47 a report, as soon as possible, in accordance with this Article. If the test results are
48 negative, all identifying information shall be obliterated if the record is retained,
49 unless the parent approves the inclusion of identifying information. Positive test
50 results shall not be admissible in a criminal prosecution.
51 (2) If there are symptoms of withdrawal in the newborn or other observable
52 and harmful effects in his physical appearance or functioning that a physician has
53 cause to believe are due to the chronic or severe use of alcohol by the mother during
54 pregnancy or are the effects of fetal alcohol spectrum disorder, the physician shall
55 issue a report in accordance with this Article.
56 H. I.(1) All instances of alleged child abuse that occur in a school setting
57 shall be immediately reported to the child's parent or legal guardian and to local or
58 state law enforcement the hotline, regardless of the alleged perpetrator.
59 (2) If more than one child is involved in the allegations, the school shall
60 immediately report to the parent or legal guardian of all involved children.
61 (3) Law enforcement shall begin an investigation of the allegations within
62 forty-eight hours of receiving the report.
Page 84 of 111

SCASB462 3005 1692
1 (4) If more than one child is involved in the allegations, law enforcement
2 shall interview the parent or legal guardian of all children involved.
3 (5) Any sexual abuse cases in which the alleged perpetrator is a child shall
4 be referred to the Department of Children and Family Services. The department shall
5 assess the family of the child victim and the alleged child perpetrator to ensure child
6 safety and well-being in accordance with Children's Code Article 612(A)(3).
7 (6) For purposes of this Article, the following definitions shall apply:
8 (a) "School setting" means in a school building, on school grounds, in school
9 vehicles, or at any activities sponsored by a school.
10 (b) "Sexual abuse" means the perpetration or attempted perpetration of R.S.
11 14:41, 42, 42.1, 43, 43.1, 43.2, 43.3, 43.4, 80, 81, 81.1, 81.2, 86, 89, or 89.1.
12 J. If a mandatory reporter is prohibited from immediately making the
13 report required by this Chapter because of an employer's policies or employee
14 manual, the mandatory reporter shall file a complaint with state police. State
15 police shall investigate the complaint, and an employer violating this Chapter
16 shall be subject to the penalties provided for in R.S. 14:131.1 and 403. An
17 employer shall not discriminate or retaliate against an employee who is a
18 mandatory reporter for complying with this Article. If an employer is found
19 discriminating or retaliating against an employee for complying with this
20 Article, the employer shall be subject to double the fines provided for in R.S.
21 14:131.1 and 403.

1 Art. 610.1. Assignment to investigative agency
2 A.(1) If a report of child maltreatment is accepted by the Child Abuse
3 Hotline, an investigation shall be conducted under procedures established by the
4 Louisiana Department of Health and Human Services and the office of state
5 police unless the report is accepted for triage pursuant to this Article.
6 (2) The procedures shall require the following:
7 (a) Assignment of a report of child maltreatment to the Louisiana
8 Department of Health and Human Services or the office of state police as the
9 investigating agency.
10 (b) Assignment of a report of child maltreatment to the office of state
11 police if the report involves:
12 (i) Severe child maltreatment.
13 (ii) A child who is in the custody of the Louisiana Department of Health
14 and Human Services.
15 (c) Assignment of a report of child maltreatment that qualifies for triage
16 procedures that are developed and implemented under this Article and as
17 prescribed by triage procedures in lieu of an assignment for investigation by the
18 Louisiana Department of Health and Human Services or the office of state
19 police.
20 B.(1) After the assignment of a report of child maltreatment, the
21 investigating agency shall initiate an investigation as provided pursuant to this
22 Article or follow triage procedures pursuant to this Article.
23 (2) After initiating the investigation and interviewing the alleged victim,
24 the investigating agency shall review the report of child maltreatment to
25 determine if the investigation should be administratively closed without
26 complying with the requirements of this Article regarding a complete
27 investigation.
28 (3) If an investigation is not administratively closed, the investigating
29 agency shall comply with the requirements of this Article regarding a complete
30 investigation.
31 C. The investigating agency shall administratively close an investigation
32 under procedures that are established by the Louisiana Department of Health
33 and Human Services. The procedures established by the Louisiana Department
34 of Health and Human Services shall require the closure of an investigation if:
35 (1) There is no evidence to support the report of child maltreatment
36 other than the report made to the Child Abuse Hotline.
37 (2) There is insufficient detail to investigate the report of child
38 maltreatment.
39 (3) There has not been an additional report of abuse or neglect that has
40 been committed by the alleged offender who is the subject of the current report.
41 (4) The investigator reviews the prior history of child maltreatment
42 related to the family of the child and to the alleged offender and determines that
43 the health and safety of the child can be assured without further investigation
44 by the Department of Health and Human Services or the office of state police.
45 (5) The investigator determines that abuse or neglect of the child is
46 unsubstantiated or the finding is inconclusive and there is approval to close the
47 investigation by the:
48 (a) Deputy secretary of child welfare of the Louisiana Department of
49 Health and Human Services or his designee for the administrative closure of an
50 investigation that is conducted by the Louisiana Department of Health and
51 Human Services.
52 (b) Superintendent of state police or his designee for the administrative
53 closure of an investigation conducted by the office of state police.
54 D.(1) The Louisiana Department of Health and Human Services and the
55 office of state police may develop and implement triage procedures for
56 accepting, documenting, and assigning reports of child maltreatment.
57 (2) The Louisiana Department of Health and Human Services and the
58 office of state police shall not implement this Article until rules necessary to
59 carry out this subsection have been promulgated pursuant to the Administrative
60 Procedure Act. Such rules may be promulgated by emergency rulemaking.
61 (3) The procedures established in accordance with this Article shall
62 assess the safety of a child upon the receipt of an accepted child maltreatment
Page 86 of 111

SCASB462 3005 1692
1 report. The assessment shall include each underlying issue or additional child
2 maltreatment concern that may not have been identified in the original Child
3 Abuse Hotline report.
4 E. The Louisiana Department of Health and Human Services shall work
5 with families related to an accepted child maltreatment report to remedy the
6 conditions or issues that resulted in the child maltreatment report.
7 Art. 610.2. Initiation of investigations
8 A. The Louisiana Department of Health and Human Services and the
9 office of state police shall cause an investigation to be made upon receiving
10 initial notification of suspected child maltreatment or notification of a child
11 death.
12 B. Except as provided in Paragraph C of this Article, all investigations
13 shall begin within seventy-two hours.
14 C. An investigation shall begin within twenty-four hours if:
15 (1) The allegation is severe maltreatment, excluding an allegation:
16 (a) Of sexual abuse if the most recent allegation of sexual abuse was
17 more than one year ago or the alleged victim does not currently have contact
18 with the alleged offender.
19 (b) Of abandonment and the child is in a facility.
20 (c) Of cuts, welts, bruises, or suffocation if the most recent allegation was
21 more than one year ago and the alleged victim is in the custody of the Louisiana
22 Department of Health and Human Services.
23 (d) In which the alleged victim is in a facility and does not currently have
24 contact with the alleged offender.
25 (2) The allegation is that a child has been subjected to neglect as defined
26 in this Part.
27 (3) A child has died suddenly and unexpectedly.
28 D. At the initial time of contact with the alleged offender, the person
29 conducting the investigation shall advise the alleged offender of the allegations
30 made against the alleged offender in a manner that is consistent with the laws
31 protecting the rights of the person who made the report.
32 E. The Louisiana Department of Health and Human Services and the
33 office of state police shall:
34 (1) Develop policy and procedures to follow when a child dies suddenly
35 and unexpectedly to use in a child death investigation.
36 (2) Determine during the Louisiana Department of Health and Human
37 Services' and the office of state police's investigation whether the child's death
38 was caused by child maltreatment.
39 (3) Assess the home to ensure the safety of surviving siblings or children
40 in the home.
41 F. Upon initiation of the investigation, the primary focus of the
42 investigation shall be whether or not the alleged offender has access to children
43 and whether or not children are at risk such that children need to be protected.
44 Art. 610.3. Reports to the United States Department of Defense Family
45 Advocacy Program
46 In an investigation of a report of abuse or neglect allegedly committed
47 by a parent or caretaker, the department shall determine whether the person
48 is an active duty member of the United States Armed Forces or the spouse of a
49 member on active duty. If the department determines that the person is an
50 active duty member of the United States Armed Forces or the spouse of a
51 member on active duty, the department shall notify the United States
52 Department of Defense Family Advocacy Program at the closest active duty
53 military installation of the investigation.

36 Art. 615. Disposition of reports
37 * * *
38 E. When after the investigation of a report, the determination is made that the
39 report is inconclusive or unsubstantiated, as provided in Subparagraphs (B)(4) and
40 (5) of this Article, the files, records, and pertinent information regarding the report
41 and investigation shall be strictly confidential, shall not become part of the central
42 registry except as otherwise provided in Subparagraph (1) of this Paragraph or in
43 Article 616(F), shall not be disclosed or ordered to be produced in conjunction with
44 any legal proceeding or other matter except as provided in Subparagraph (4) of this
45 Paragraph, and shall be maintained only for the following purposes:
46 (1) The files, records, and information shall remain unsealed and shall be
47 maintained for the exclusive use of child protective services, to assist in future risk
48 and safety assessments. The Louisiana Department of Children and Family Services
49 Health and Human Services shall maintain all files and records for seven years
50 from the date of the determination, unless a subsequent inconclusive or
51 unsubstantiated report is received during that period. In that case, information from
52 all such reports will be maintained until the youngest child in the alleged victim's
53 family attains the age of eighteen years or seven years from the date of the latest
54 determination, whichever is longer. If information from an inconclusive or
55 unsubstantiated report is used as a part of the basis for a later, related, and
56 substantiated report, the earlier report shall become part of the file of the
57 substantiated report and shall cease to be a separate report.
58 (2) All files, records, and information shall be admissible in any civil
59 litigation or criminal proceeding against the Louisiana Department of Children and
60 Family Services Health and Human Services or its employees wherein work
61 performance or conduct is at issue. They shall remain confidential and be placed
62 under seal by the court to prevent disclosure to the public. The department shall
Page 88 of 111

SCASB462 3005 1692
1 maintain the files, records and information during the pendency of the litigation or
2 prosecution.

7 Art. 725. Findings and purpose
8 The legislature finds that arresting, prosecuting, and incarcerating victimized
9 children serves to re-traumatize them and to increase their feelings of low self-
10 esteem, which only makes the process of recovery more difficult. Both federal and
11 international law recognize that sexually exploited children are the victims of crime
12 and should be treated as such. Therefore, sexually exploited children should not be
13 prosecuted for criminal acts related to prostitution. Instead, sexually exploited
14 children should, where possible, be diverted into services that address the needs of
15 these children outside of the justice system. Sexually exploited children deserve the
16 protection of child welfare services, including diversion, crisis intervention,
17 counseling, and emergency housing services. The purpose of this Chapter is to
18 protect a child from further victimization after the child is discovered to be a
19 sexually exploited child by ensuring that a child protective response is in place in the
20 state. This is to be accomplished by presuming that any child engaged in prostitution,
21 prostitution by massage, or crime against nature by solicitation is a victim of sex
22 trafficking and providing these children with the appropriate care and services where
23 possible. In determining the need for and capacity of services that may be provided,
24 the Louisiana Department of Children and Family Services Health and Human
25 Services shall recognize that sexually exploited children have separate and distinct
26 service needs according to gender, and every effort should be made to ensure these
27 children are not prosecuted or treated as juvenile delinquents, but instead are given
28 the appropriate social services.
29 Art. 725.1. Definitions
30 As used in this Chapter, the following terms and phrases shall have the
31 following meaning, unless the context requires otherwise:
32 (1) "Department" means the Louisiana Department of Children and Family
33 Services Health and Human Services.

45 Art. 811.1. Rights of the victim of alleged delinquent act
46 * * *
47 F.(1) In order to protect the identity and provide for the safety and welfare
48 of juvenile crime victims under the age of eighteen years, all public officials and
49 officers and public agencies, including but not limited to all law enforcement
50 agencies, sheriffs, district attorneys, judicial officers, clerks of court, and the
51 Louisiana Department of Children and Family Services Health and Human
52 Services or any division thereof, shall not publicly disclose the name, address, or
53 identity of a juvenile victim of crime who at the time of the commission of the
54 offense is under eighteen years of age. The public disclosure of the name of the
55 juvenile crime victim by any public official or officer or public agency is not
56 prohibited by this Subparagraph when the crime resulted in the death of the victim.
57 (2) Notwithstanding any other provision of law to the contrary, all public
58 officials, officers, and public agencies, including but not limited to all law
59 enforcement agencies, sheriffs, district attorneys, judicial officers, clerks of court,
60 and the Louisiana Department of Children and Family Services Health and Human
61 Services or any division thereof, charged with the responsibility of knowing the
62 name, address, and identity of juvenile crime victims as a necessary part of their
Page 91 of 111

SCASB462 3005 1692
1 duties shall have full and complete access to this information regarding a juvenile
2 crime victim, and they may lawfully utilize initials, abbreviations, or other forms of
3 indefinite descriptions on all public documents used in the performance of their
4 duties to whatever extent they deem necessary, to prevent the public disclosure of the
5 name, address, or identity of a juvenile victim of crime under the age of eighteen
6 years.
7 G.(1) In order to protect the identity and provide for the safety and welfare
8 of juvenile crime victims under the age of seventeen years, all public officials and
9 officers and public agencies, including but not limited to all law enforcement
10 agencies, sheriffs, district attorneys, judicial officers, clerks of court, and the
11 Louisiana Department of Children and Family Services Health and Human
12 Services or any division thereof, shall not publicly disclose the name, address, or
13 identity of a juvenile victim of crime who at the time of the commission of the
14 offense is under seventeen years of age. The public disclosure of the name of the
15 juvenile crime victim by any public official or officer or public agency is not
16 prohibited by this Subparagraph when the crime resulted in the death of the victim.
17 (2) Notwithstanding any other provision of law to the contrary, all public
18 officials, officers, and public agencies, including but not limited to all law
19 enforcement agencies, sheriffs, district attorneys, judicial officers, clerks of court,
20 and the Louisiana Department of Children and Family Services Health and Human
21 Services or any division thereof, charged with the responsibility of knowing the
22 name, address and identity of juvenile crime victims as a necessary part of their
23 duties shall have full and complete access to this information regarding a juvenile
24 crime victim and they may lawfully utilize initials, abbreviations, or other forms of
25 indefinite descriptions on all public documents used in the performance of their
26 duties to whatever extent they deem necessary, to prevent the public disclosure of the
27 name, address, or identity of a juvenile victim of crime under the age of seventeen
28 years.
29 * * *
30 Art. 822. Place of continued custody prior to adjudication
31 * * *
32 B. The court shall not place a child alleged to be delinquent in the custody of
33 either the department of Children and Family Services Louisiana Department of
34 Health and Human Services or the department Department of Public Safety and
35 Corrections prior to adjudication.

55 Art. 1109. Domiciliary requirements
56 A surrendering parent must be domiciled in this state for at least eight
57 months, unless a prospective adoptive parent has been domiciled in this state for at
58 least eight months, or the child is in the custody of the Louisiana Department of
59 Children and Family Services Health and Human Services.

24 Art. 1127.1. Maintenance of medical report; transfer of adoption records
25 * * *
26 D. After the final decree of adoption, if the firm or lawyer is unable to
27 assume ongoing responsibility for the continuing duty pursuant to this Article, it
28 shall transfer its adoption records to the Louisiana Department of Children and
29 Family Services Health and Human Services or another transferee approved by the
30 department. Thereafter, that transferee shall assume the continuing duty imposed by
31 this Article. Should any client subsequently attempt to update information, the firm
32 or lawyer shall refer the client to the current custodian of the record, and if
33 appropriate, to the voluntary registry.

2 Art. 1180. Venue and jurisdiction in adoption
3 * * *
4 C. Upon filing of the act of voluntary surrender approved by the court
5 according to Article 1131(C), the court of competent venue and jurisdiction wherein
6 the surrender is filed shall have exclusive, original jurisdiction over all issues of
7 custody and adoption of the child during the pendency of the proceedings, unless the
8 child is in the custody of the Louisiana Department of Children and Family Services
9 Health.
10 * * *
11 Art. 1182. Records of adoption decrees
12 A. Whenever an interlocutory decree of adoption has been granted, the clerk
13 of court shall forward a certified copy of the decree to the Louisiana Department of
14 Social Services Health and Human Services.
15 B. Whenever a final decree of adoption has been granted with regard to a
16 child born in Louisiana, the clerk of court shall forward, on a form supplied by the
17 Louisiana Department of Children and Family Services Health and Human
18 Services, a certificate of the decree to the state registrar of vital records.
19 * * *
20 Art. 1186. Confidential adoption records; disclosure
21 * * *
22 B. If the agency, firm, or lawyer ceases to do business in this state, it shall
23 transfer its adoption records to the Louisiana Department of Children and Family
24 Services Health and Human Services or another transferee approved by the
25 department. Thereafter, the transferee shall ensure the preservation and
26 confidentiality of records required by Paragraph A of this Article and assumes
27 responsibility for providing nonidentifying information as required by Articles 1127
28 and 1127.1.

35 respective counsel review this Agreement.

52 must be preserved until such time as we modify them by mutual written agreement
53 or the court modifies or terminates this Agreement in accordance with Louisiana
54 Children's Code Article 1269.8.

56 always be interpreted to serve (NAME OF CHILD)'s best interest. We agree that we
57 will always attempt to resolve any disagreement that may arise in (HIS/HER) best
58 interest and acknowledge that court modification or enforcement is to be used only
59 as a last resort when all informal means of resolution have been exhausted. We

61 hear a motion to enforce, modify, or terminate this Agreement only after we have

30 Art. 1270. Legislative findings; purpose; release of information
31 * * *
32 B. There is hereby created within the office of children and family services
33 of the child welfare, Louisiana Department of Children and Family Services Health
34 and Human Services a voluntary registry for the matching of adopted persons, or
35 an adoptive parent of a minor or deceased adopted person, or a descendant of a
36 deceased adopted person, or his parent if a minor, and biological parents or siblings,
37 or both, or a parent, sibling, or descendant, or his parent if a minor, of a deceased
38 biological parent. The purpose of this registry shall be to facilitate voluntary contact
39 between the adopted person, or an adoptive parent of a minor or deceased adopted
40 person, or the descendant of a deceased adopted person, or his parent if a minor, and
41 a biological parent or biological sibling, or both, or a parent, sibling, or descendant,
42 or his parent if a minor, of a deceased biological parent.
43 * * *
44 Art. 1274. Penalties
45 Any employee or former employee of the Louisiana Department of Children
46 and Family Services Health and Human Services, or a licensed adoption agency,
47 or any employee or appointee or former employee or appointee of a court who
48 discloses identifying information other than pursuant to judicial order or through the
49 registry, as provided in this Chapter, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be
50 fined not less than five hundred dollars and not more than five thousand dollars, or
51 imprisoned for not more than six months, or both.

8 Art. 1282.5. Change of name
9 The full name of the adopted child may be changed in the final decree of
10 adoption and, if changed, the surname shall be the same as that of the adoptive
11 parent. In accordance with R.S. 40:79, the clerk of court shall forward, on a form
12 supplied by the Louisiana Department of Children and Family Services Health and
13 Human Services, his certificate of the decree to the state registrar, who shall make
14 a new certificate of live birth of the person adopted, in the new name if the name has
15 been changed in the decree.

61 Art. 1518. Pretrial orders; contribution to costs; appointment of counsel; Indian
62 parent or custodian
Page 109 of 111

SCASB462 3005 1692
1 * * *
2 B. Upon request of an indigent parent, the court shall appoint counsel for the
3 parent when the Louisiana Department of Children and Family Services Health and
4 Human Services has recommended that the petition for voluntary transfer be filed.
5 * * *
6 Art. 1519. Hearing
7 The petition shall be set for hearing on the record unless specifically waived
8 by the court. If the Louisiana Department of Children and Family Services Health
9 and Human Services, office of children and family services, child welfare, has
10 recommended that the petition for voluntary transfer of custody be filed, a
11 representative for the department shall testify at the hearing with particularity the
12 reasons for the recommendation. Further, the department representative shall specify
13 why a child in need of care petition should not be filed and shall testify regarding the
14 preventative services offered by the department to the petitioner to prevent the
15 transfer of custody.
16 Art. 1567. Venue; standing
17 * * *
18 B. An adult may seek relief under this Chapter by filing a petition with the
19 court alleging abuse by the defendant. Any parent, adult household member, local
20 child protection unit of the Louisiana Department of Children and Family Services
21 Health and Human Services, or district attorney may seek relief on behalf of any
22 child or any person alleged to be incompetent by filing a petition with the court
23 alleging abuse by the defendant. A petitioner's right to relief under this Chapter shall
24 not be affected by his leaving the residence or household to avoid further abuse.
25 * * *
26 Art. 1641. Rulemaking authority; effect of rules
27 A. The Louisiana Department of Children and Family Services Health and
28 Human Services shall have the authority to promulgate rules and regulations in
29 accordance with the Administrative Procedure Act as necessary to carry out the
30 provisions of this Chapter.

45 applicable to the programs and operations transferred from the Department of Children and
46 Family Services to the Louisiana Department of Health and Human Services, the
47 Department of Justice, and the office of state police by this Act shall continue to be effective,
48 and the office of state register shall change all applicable references to the Department of
49 Children and Family Services to the Louisiana Department of Health and Human Services,
50 Department of Justice, or office of state police as applicable, and redesignate and renumber,
51 as needed, all applicable provisions as are necessary to maintain continuity in the Louisiana
52 Administrative Code.
53 Section 32.(A) All Department of Children and Family Services contracts related to
54 the operation and administration of the programs and activities transferred to the Louisiana
55 Department of Health and Human Services, the Department of Justice, and the office of state
56 police by this Act shall be deemed to have been transferred and assigned to the Louisiana
57 Department of Health and Human Services, the Department of Justice, and the office of state
58 police upon the effective date of this Section without the necessity of contractual
59 amendment, and the Louisiana Department of Health and Human Services the Department
60 of Justice, and the office of state police shall be responsible for all related obligations and
61 liabilities arising on or after that effective date.

1 (B) In order to ensure continuity of services during the transition period, any pending
2 or unfinished business of the programs being transferred over shall be taken over and
3 completed the Louisiana Department of Health and Human Services, the Department of
4 Justice, and the office of state police with the same power and authorization as that of the
5 Department of Children and Family Services.
6 (C)(1) All employees engaged in the performance of duties relating to the functions
7 of the programs and services transferred from the Department of Children and Family
8 Services to the Louisiana Department of Health and Human Services, the Department of
9 Justice, and the office of state police are hereby transferred to carry out the functions of the
10 transferred programs and services and shall continue to perform their duties, subject to
11 applicable state civil service laws, rules, and regulations. Subject to such laws, positions in
12 the unclassified service shall remain in the unclassified service. Upon the transfer of
13 employees to a board, such employees shall immediately have the ability to payroll deduct
14 or direct deposit their payroll earnings in favor of any credit union of which they were
15 members prior to the transfer.
16 (2) The Department of State Civil Service shall assist the Department of Children and
17 Family Services, and the Louisiana Department of Health and Human Services, the
18 Department of Justice, and the office of state police in all human resource activities deemed
19 necessary to make such a transfer. All human resource activities shall include but are not
20 limited to the transfer of personnel files and other related confidential documents, position
21 descriptions, retirement benefits, and related benefits, including but not limited to those
22 offered by the Office of Group Benefits.
23 Section 33. The Louisiana State Law Institute is hereby directed to replace all
24 references to the "Louisiana Department of Health" to the "Louisiana Department of Health
25 and Human Services" in the Louisiana Revised Statutes of 1950 and applicable Codes.
26 Section 34. All employees engaged in the performance of duties relating to the
27 functions of accounting and budget control, procurement and contract management, data
28 processing, personnel management, and grants management shall transfer to the Louisiana
29 Department of Health and Human Services on July 1, 2026.
30 Section 35.(A) This Section and Section 34 of this Act shall become effective upon
31 signature by the governor or, if not signed by the governor, upon expiration of the time for
32 bills to become law without signature by the governor, as provided by Article III, Section
33 18 of the Constitution of Louisiana. If vetoed by the governor and subsequently approved
34 by the legislature, this Act shall become effective on the day following such approval.
35 (B) Sections 1 through 33 of this Act shall become effective on October 1, 2026."
